<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">Princess Louise, Duchess of Argyll</h1>
<div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
<div id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
<div id="contentSub"></div>
<div class="mw-jump" id="jump-to-nav">

<p><b>Princess Louise, Duchess of Argyll</b>, <span style="font-size:100%;"><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lady_of_the_Royal_Order_of_Victoria_and_Albert" title="Lady of the Royal Order of Victoria and Albert">VA</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Companion_of_the_Order_of_the_Crown_of_India" title="Companion of the Order of the Crown of India">CI</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dame_Grand_Cross_of_the_Royal_Victorian_Order" title="Dame Grand Cross of the Royal Victorian Order">GCVO</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dame_Grand_Cross_of_the_Order_of_the_British_Empire" title="Dame Grand Cross of the Order of the British Empire">GBE</a>, <a href="/wiki/Royal_Red_Cross" title="Royal Red Cross">RRC</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dame_Grand_Cross_of_the_Order_of_St_John" title="Dame Grand Cross of the Order of St John">GCStJ</a></span> (Louise Caroline Alberta; 18 March 1848 – 3 December 1939), was the sixth child and fourth daughter of <a href="/wiki/Queen_Victoria" title="Queen Victoria">Queen Victoria</a> and <a href="/wiki/Albert,_Prince_Consort" title="Albert, Prince Consort">Prince Albert</a>.</p>
<p>Her early life was spent moving among the various <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_British_Royal_Residences" title="List of British Royal Residences">royal residences</a> in the company of her family. When her father, the Prince Consort, died on 14 December 1861, the court went into a period of intense mourning, to which Louise was unsympathetic. Louise was an able <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sculptor" title="Sculptor">sculptor</a> and artist, and several of her sculptures remain today. She was also a supporter of the <a href="/wiki/Feminist_movement" title="Feminist movement">feminist movement</a>, corresponded with <a href="/wiki/Josephine_Butler" title="Josephine Butler">Josephine Butler</a>, and visited <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_Garrett_Anderson" title="Elizabeth Garrett Anderson">Elizabeth Garrett</a>. She held that "the subject of Domestic Economy lies at the root of the – highest life of every true woman."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMorgan19031_1-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMorgan19031-1">[1]</a></sup></p>
<p>Before her marriage, Louise served as an unofficial secretary to her mother, the Queen (1866–1871). The question of Louise's marriage was discussed in the late 1860s. Suitors from the royal houses of <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Prussia" title="Kingdom of Prussia">Prussia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Denmark" title="Denmark">Denmark</a> were suggested, but Victoria wanted new blood in the family and therefore suggested a high-ranking member of the <a href="/wiki/Aristocracy" title="Aristocracy">aristocracy</a>. Despite opposition from members of the royal family, Louise fell in love with <a href="/wiki/John_Campbell,_9th_Duke_of_Argyll" title="John Campbell, 9th Duke of Argyll">John, Marquess of Lorne</a>, the heir to the <a href="/wiki/Duke_of_Argyll" title="Duke of Argyll">Duke of Argyll</a>, and Victoria consented to the marriage,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-London_Gazette_25_October_1870_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-London_Gazette_25_October_1870-2">[2]</a></sup> which took place on 21 March 1871.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-London_Gazette_24_March_1871_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-London_Gazette_24_March_1871-3">[3]</a></sup> Despite a happy beginning, the two drifted apart, possibly because of their childlessness and the Queen's constraints on their activities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStocker_2004.2C_Louise.2C_Princess.2C_duchess_of_Argyll_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStocker_2004.2C_Louise.2C_Princess.2C_duchess_of_Argyll-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1878, Lorne was appointed <a href="/wiki/Governor_General_of_Canada" title="Governor General of Canada">Governor General of Canada</a>. Louise became viceregal consort, but her stay was unhappy as a result of homesickness and dislike of <a href="/wiki/Ottawa" title="Ottawa">Ottawa</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStocker_2004.2C_Louise.2C_Princess.2C_duchess_of_Argyll_4-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStocker_2004.2C_Louise.2C_Princess.2C_duchess_of_Argyll-4">[4]</a></sup> Following Victoria's death in 1901, Louise entered the social circle established by her brother, the new king, <a href="/wiki/Edward_VII" title="Edward VII">Edward VII</a>. Louise's marriage survived thanks to long periods of separation, but the couple reconciled in 1911, and she was devastated by her husband's death in 1914. After the end of the <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">First World War</a> in 1918, at the age of 70, she began to retire from public life, undertaking few public duties outside <a href="/wiki/Kensington_Palace" title="Kensington Palace">Kensington Palace</a>, where she died at age 91.</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life">Early life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Princess_Louise,_Duchess_of_Argyll&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Early life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Henrietta_Montalba.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="515" data-file-width="414" height="211" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Henrietta_Montalba.jpg/170px-Henrietta_Montalba.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Henrietta_Montalba.jpg/255px-Henrietta_Montalba.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Henrietta_Montalba.jpg/340px-Henrietta_Montalba.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Henrietta_Montalba.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Portrait of <a href="/wiki/Henrietta_Montalba" title="Henrietta Montalba">Henrietta Montalba</a> painted by Princess Louise in 1882</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Louise was born on 18 March 1848 at <a href="/wiki/Buckingham_Palace" title="Buckingham Palace">Buckingham Palace</a>, <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarshall1972122_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarshall1972122-5">[5]</a></sup> She was the fourth daughter and sixth child of the reigning British monarch, <a href="/wiki/Queen_Victoria" title="Queen Victoria">Queen Victoria</a>, and her husband <a href="/wiki/Albert,_Prince_Consort" title="Albert, Prince Consort">Prince Albert of Saxe-Coburg and Gotha</a>. As the daughter of the sovereign, Louise was styled <i><a href="/wiki/Royal_Highness" title="Royal Highness">Her Royal Highness</a> The Princess Louise</i> from birth. Her birth coincided with <a href="/wiki/Revolutions_of_1848" title="Revolutions of 1848">revolutions</a> which swept across <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a>, prompting the Queen to remark that Louise would turn out to be "something peculiar".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELongford1987195_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELongford1987195-6">[6]</a></sup> The Queen's labour with Louise was the first to be aided with <a href="/wiki/Chloroform" title="Chloroform">chloroform</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELongford1987195_6-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELongford1987195-6">[6]</a></sup></p>
<p>Albert and Victoria chose the names <i>Louisa Caroline Alberta</i>. Louise was chosen to honour <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Louise_of_Saxe-Gotha-Altenburg" title="Louise of Saxe-Gotha-Altenburg">Albert's mother</a>. Though christened Louisa in Buckingham Palace's private chapel by <a href="/wiki/John_Bird_Sumner" title="John Bird Sumner">John Bird Sumner</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Archbishop_of_Canterbury" title="Archbishop of Canterbury">Archbishop of Canterbury</a>, on 13 May 1848, she was invariably known as Louise throughout her life.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-London_Gazette_17_May_1848_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-London_Gazette_17_May_1848-7">[7]</a></sup> Her godparents were Duke Gustav of Mecklenburg-Schwerin (her paternal great-great-uncle, for whom Prince Albert stood proxy); <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Marie_Fredericka_of_Hesse-Kassel" title="Marie Fredericka of Hesse-Kassel">The Duchess of Saxe-Meiningen</a> (for whom her great-aunt <a href="/wiki/Adelaide_of_Saxe-Meiningen" title="Adelaide of Saxe-Meiningen">Queen Adelaide</a> stood proxy); and <a href="/wiki/Princess_Augusta_of_Cambridge" title="Princess Augusta of Cambridge">The Hereditary Grand Duchess of Mecklenburg-Strelitz</a> (her first cousin once-removed, for whom the Hereditary Grand Duchess's mother <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Princess_Augusta_of_Hesse-Cassel" title="Princess Augusta of Hesse-Cassel">The Duchess of Cambridge</a> stood proxy).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-London_Gazette_17_May_1848_7-1"><a href="#cite_note-London_Gazette_17_May_1848-7">[7]</a></sup> During the ceremony, <a href="/wiki/Princess_Mary,_Duchess_of_Gloucester_and_Edinburgh" title="Princess Mary, Duchess of Gloucester and Edinburgh">The Duchess of Gloucester</a>, one of the few children of <a href="/wiki/George_III_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="George III of the United Kingdom">George III</a> who was still alive, forgot where she was, and suddenly got up in the middle of the service and knelt at the Queen's feet, much to the Queen's horror.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELongford1987195_6-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELongford1987195-6">[6]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Queen_Victoria_(1819-1901),_after_Franz_Xavier_Winterhalter_-_Portrait_of_Princess_Louise_(1848-1939).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1034" data-file-width="994" height="229" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Queen_Victoria_%281819-1901%29%2C_after_Franz_Xavier_Winterhalter_-_Portrait_of_Princess_Louise_%281848-1939%29.jpg/220px-Queen_Victoria_%281819-1901%29%2C_after_Franz_Xavier_Winterhalter_-_Portrait_of_Princess_Louise_%281848-1939%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Queen_Victoria_%281819-1901%29%2C_after_Franz_Xavier_Winterhalter_-_Portrait_of_Princess_Louise_%281848-1939%29.jpg/330px-Queen_Victoria_%281819-1901%29%2C_after_Franz_Xavier_Winterhalter_-_Portrait_of_Princess_Louise_%281848-1939%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Queen_Victoria_%281819-1901%29%2C_after_Franz_Xavier_Winterhalter_-_Portrait_of_Princess_Louise_%281848-1939%29.jpg/440px-Queen_Victoria_%281819-1901%29%2C_after_Franz_Xavier_Winterhalter_-_Portrait_of_Princess_Louise_%281848-1939%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Queen_Victoria_(1819-1901),_after_Franz_Xavier_Winterhalter_-_Portrait_of_Princess_Louise_(1848-1939).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Queen Victoria painted a portrait of Princess Louise after an original by <a href="/wiki/Franz_Xaver_Winterhalter" title="Franz Xaver Winterhalter">Franz Xaver Winterhalter</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Like her siblings, Louise was brought up with the strict programme of education devised by her father, Prince Albert, and his friend and confidant, <a href="/wiki/Christian_Friedrich,_Baron_Stockmar" title="Christian Friedrich, Baron Stockmar">Baron Stockmar</a>. The young children were taught practical tasks, such as cooking, farming, household tasks and carpentry.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMart.C3.ADnez2005_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMart.C3.ADnez2005-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<p>From her early years, Louise was a talented and intelligent child, and her artistic talents were quickly recognised.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERalph_Lewis1996_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERalph_Lewis1996-9">[9]</a></sup> On his visit to <a href="/wiki/Osborne_House" title="Osborne House">Osborne House</a> in 1863, <a href="/wiki/Hallam_Tennyson,_2nd_Baron_Tennyson" title="Hallam Tennyson, 2nd Baron Tennyson">Hallam Tennyson</a>, the son of the poet <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alfred_Tennyson,_1st_Baron_Tennyson" title="Alfred Tennyson, 1st Baron Tennyson">Alfred, Lord Tennyson</a>, remarked that Louise could "draw beautifully".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> Because of her royal rank, an artistic career was not considered. However, the Queen first allowed her to attend art school under the tutelage of the sculptor <a href="/wiki/Mary_Thornycroft" title="Mary Thornycroft">Mary Thornycroft</a>, and later (1863) allowed her to study at the <a href="/wiki/Royal_College_of_Art" title="Royal College of Art">National Art Training School</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/South_Kensington" title="South Kensington">South Kensington</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStocker_2004.2C_Louise.2C_Princess.2C_duchess_of_Argyll_4-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStocker_2004.2C_Louise.2C_Princess.2C_duchess_of_Argyll-4">[4]</a></sup> Louise also became an able dancer, and Victoria wrote, after a dance, that Louise "danced <a href="/wiki/Scottish_sword_dances" title="Scottish sword dances">the sword dance</a> with more verve and accuracy than any of her sisters".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcDougall_1988.2C_Youth_.281848.E2.80.931878.29_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcDougall_1988.2C_Youth_.281848.E2.80.931878.29-12">[12]</a></sup> Her wit and intelligence made her a favourite with her father,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECantelupe1949_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECantelupe1949-13">[13]</a></sup> with her inquisitive nature earning her the nickname "Little Miss Why" from other members of the royal family.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcDougall_1988.2C_Youth_.281848.E2.80.931878.29_12-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcDougall_1988.2C_Youth_.281848.E2.80.931878.29-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Princess_Louise_(1848-1939)_and_Louise_van_de_Weyer_by_James_Valentine_(1815-1879).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1205" data-file-width="736" height="360" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f6/Princess_Louise_%281848-1939%29_and_Louise_van_de_Weyer_by_James_Valentine_%281815-1879%29.jpg/220px-Princess_Louise_%281848-1939%29_and_Louise_van_de_Weyer_by_James_Valentine_%281815-1879%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f6/Princess_Louise_%281848-1939%29_and_Louise_van_de_Weyer_by_James_Valentine_%281815-1879%29.jpg/330px-Princess_Louise_%281848-1939%29_and_Louise_van_de_Weyer_by_James_Valentine_%281815-1879%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f6/Princess_Louise_%281848-1939%29_and_Louise_van_de_Weyer_by_James_Valentine_%281815-1879%29.jpg/440px-Princess_Louise_%281848-1939%29_and_Louise_van_de_Weyer_by_James_Valentine_%281815-1879%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Princess_Louise_(1848-1939)_and_Louise_van_de_Weyer_by_James_Valentine_(1815-1879).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Princess Louise and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sylvain_van_de_Weyer" title="Sylvain van de Weyer">Louise van de Weyer</a> (died 1896) by <a href="/wiki/James_Valentine_(photographer)" title="James Valentine (photographer)">James Valentine</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> circa 1866-1870.</div>
</div>
</div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Death_of_Prince_Albert">Death of Prince Albert</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Princess_Louise,_Duchess_of_Argyll&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Death of Prince Albert">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Louise_1860s.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="555" data-file-width="435" height="217" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Louise_1860s.jpg/170px-Louise_1860s.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Louise_1860s.jpg/255px-Louise_1860s.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Louise_1860s.jpg/340px-Louise_1860s.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Louise_1860s.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Princess Louise in the 1860s</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Louise's father, Prince Albert, died at Windsor on 14 December 1861. The Queen was devastated, and ordered her household to move from Windsor to <a href="/wiki/Osborne_House" title="Osborne House">Osborne House</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Isle_of_Wight" title="Isle of Wight">Isle of Wight</a>. The atmosphere of the royal court became gloomy and morbid in the wake of the Prince's death, and entertainments became dry and dull.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDennison200773_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDennison200773-15">[15]</a></sup> Louise quickly became dissatisfied with her mother's prolonged mourning.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDennison200773_15-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDennison200773-15">[15]</a></sup> For her seventeenth birthday in 1865, Louise requested the ballroom to be opened for a <a href="/wiki/Debutante" title="Debutante">debutante</a> dance, the like of which had not been performed since Prince Albert's death. Her request was refused, and her boredom with the mundane routine of travelling between the different royal residences at set times irritated her mother, who considered Louise to be indiscreet and argumentative.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStocker_2004.2C_Louise.2C_Princess.2C_duchess_of_Argyll_4-3"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStocker_2004.2C_Louise.2C_Princess.2C_duchess_of_Argyll-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Queen comforted herself by rigidly continuing with Prince Albert's plans for their children. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alice_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Alice of the United Kingdom">Princess Alice</a> was married to <a href="/wiki/Louis_IV,_Grand_Duke_of_Hesse" title="Louis IV, Grand Duke of Hesse">Prince Louis</a>, the future <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Grand_Duke_of_Hesse" title="Grand Duke of Hesse">Grand Duke of Hesse</a>, at <a href="/wiki/Osborne_House" title="Osborne House">Osborne</a> on 1 June 1862. In 1863, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Edward_VII_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Edward VII of the United Kingdom">Edward</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Prince_of_Wales" title="Prince of Wales">Prince of Wales</a>, married <a href="/wiki/Alexandra_of_Denmark" title="Alexandra of Denmark">Princess Alexandra of Denmark</a>. The Queen made it a tradition that the eldest unmarried daughter would become her unofficial secretary, a position which Louise filled in 1866, despite the Queen's concern that she was indiscreet.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDennison200773_15-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDennison200773-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<p>Louise, however, proved to be good at the job: Victoria wrote shortly afterwards: "She is (and who would some years ago have thought it?) a clever dear girl with a fine strong character, unselfish and affectionate."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> However, when Louise fell in love with her brother Leopold's tutor, the Reverend <a href="/wiki/Robinson_Duckworth" title="Robinson Duckworth">Robinson Duckworth</a> (14 years her senior), between 1866 and 1870, the Queen reacted by dismissing Duckworth in 1870. He later became <a href="/wiki/Canon_(priest)" title="Canon (priest)">Canon</a> of <a href="/wiki/Westminster_Abbey" title="Westminster Abbey">Westminster Abbey</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChomet199920.E2.80.9321_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChomet199920.E2.80.9321-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<p>Louise was bored at court, and by fulfilling her duties, which were little more than minor secretarial tasks, such as writing letters on the Queen's behalf; dealing with political correspondence; and providing the Queen with company, she had more responsibilities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDennison2007204_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDennison2007204-18">[18]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Marriage">Marriage</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Princess_Louise,_Duchess_of_Argyll&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Marriage">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Suitors">Suitors</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Princess_Louise,_Duchess_of_Argyll&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Suitors">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>As a daughter of the Queen, Louise was a desirable bride; more so as she is regarded as the Queen's most beautiful daughter by both contemporary and modern biographers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> However, she was accused by the press, without substantiation, of romantic affairs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStocker_2004.2C_Louise.2C_Princess.2C_duchess_of_Argyll_4-4"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStocker_2004.2C_Louise.2C_Princess.2C_duchess_of_Argyll-4">[4]</a></sup> This, coupled with her <a href="/wiki/Liberalism" title="Liberalism">liberalism</a> and <a href="/wiki/Feminism" title="Feminism">feminism</a>, prompted the Queen to find her a husband. The choice had to suit Victoria as well as Louise, and the Queen insisted that her daughter's husband should live near her, a promise which had also been extracted from the husband of Helena, Louise's sister. Various suitors were proposed by the leading royal houses of Europe: <a href="/wiki/Alexandra_of_Denmark" title="Alexandra of Denmark">Princess Alexandra</a> proposed her brother, the <a href="/wiki/Frederick_VIII_of_Denmark" title="Frederick VIII of Denmark">Crown Prince of Denmark</a>, but the Queen was strongly opposed to another Danish marriage that could antagonise <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Prussia" title="Kingdom of Prussia">Prussia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Victoria,_Princess_Royal" title="Victoria, Princess Royal">Victoria</a>, Louise's eldest sister, proposed the tall and rich <a href="/wiki/Prince_Albert_of_Prussia_(1837%E2%80%931906)" title="Prince Albert of Prussia (1837–1906)">Prince Albert of Prussia</a>, but Queen Victoria disapproved of another Prussian marriage that would have been unpopular in England.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBuckle1926632_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBuckle1926632-21">[21]</a></sup> Prince Albert was also reluctant to settle in England as required. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Prince_William_of_the_Netherlands" title="Prince William of the Netherlands">William, Prince of Orange</a> was also considered a suitor, but because of his extravagant lifestyle in <a href="/wiki/Paris" title="Paris">Paris</a>, where he lived openly with a <a href="/wiki/Mistress_(lover)" title="Mistress (lover)">mistress</a>, the Queen quickly vetoed the idea.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWake1988100_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWake1988100-22">[22]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Princess_Louise_and_Lorne_engagement.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="525" data-file-width="383" height="233" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Princess_Louise_and_Lorne_engagement.jpg/170px-Princess_Louise_and_Lorne_engagement.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Princess_Louise_and_Lorne_engagement.jpg/255px-Princess_Louise_and_Lorne_engagement.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Princess_Louise_and_Lorne_engagement.jpg/340px-Princess_Louise_and_Lorne_engagement.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Princess_Louise_and_Lorne_engagement.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Princess Louise and Marquess of Lorne. The official engagement photo (W &amp; D Downey, 1870)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Louise viewed marriage to any prince as undesirable, and announced that she wished to marry <a href="/wiki/John_Campbell,_9th_Duke_of_Argyll" title="John Campbell, 9th Duke of Argyll">John Campbell</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Marquess_of_Lorne" title="Marquess of Lorne">Marquess of Lorne</a>, heir to the <a href="/wiki/Duke_of_Argyll" title="Duke of Argyll">Dukedom of Argyll</a>. No such marriage, between a daughter of a Sovereign and a British subject, had been given official recognition since 1515, when <a href="/wiki/Charles_Brandon,_1st_Duke_of_Suffolk" title="Charles Brandon, 1st Duke of Suffolk">Charles Brandon</a>, the first <a href="/wiki/Duke_of_Suffolk" title="Duke of Suffolk">Duke of Suffolk</a>, married <a href="/wiki/Mary_Tudor,_Queen_of_France" title="Mary Tudor, Queen of France">Mary Tudor</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStocker_2004.2C_Louise.2C_Princess.2C_duchess_of_Argyll_4-5"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStocker_2004.2C_Louise.2C_Princess.2C_duchess_of_Argyll-4">[4]</a></sup> Louise's brother, the Prince of Wales, was strongly opposed to a marriage with a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mediatization" title="Mediatization">non-mediatized</a> noble.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBenson1938162_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBenson1938162-23">[23]</a></sup> Furthermore, Lorne's father, <a href="/wiki/George_Campbell,_8th_Duke_of_Argyll" title="George Campbell, 8th Duke of Argyll">George Campbell</a>, the eighth Duke of Argyll, was an ardent supporter of <a href="/wiki/William_Ewart_Gladstone" title="William Ewart Gladstone">William Ewart Gladstone</a>, and the Prince of Wales was worried that he would drag the royal family into political disputes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBuckle1926632_21-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBuckle1926632-21">[21]</a></sup> Nevertheless, the opposition was crushed by the Queen, who wrote to the Prince of Wales in 1869:</p>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>That which you object to [that Louise should marry a subject] <i>I feel</i> certain will be <i>for</i> Louise's happiness and for the peace and quiet of the family ... Times have changed; great foreign alliances are looked on as causes of trouble and anxiety, and are of no good. What could be more painful than the position in which our family were placed during the wars with Denmark, and between Prussia and Austria? ... You may not be aware, as I am, with what <i>dislike</i> the marriages of Princesses of the Royal Family with small German Princes (German beggars as they most insultingly were called) ... As to position, I see <i>no</i> difficulty whatever; Louise remains what she is, and her husband keeps his rank ... only being treated in the family as a relation when we are together ...<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBuckle1926632.E2.80.93633_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBuckle1926632.E2.80.93633-24">[24]</a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<p>The Queen averred that Louise's marriage to a subject would bring "<i>new blood</i>" into the family,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBuckle1926632.E2.80.93633_24-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBuckle1926632.E2.80.93633-24">[24]</a></sup> while all European princes were related to each other. She was convinced that this would strengthen the royal family morally and physically.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Engagement_and_wedding">Engagement and wedding</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Princess_Louise,_Duchess_of_Argyll&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Engagement and wedding">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Lorne.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="500" data-file-width="380" height="224" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Lorne.jpg/170px-Lorne.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Lorne.jpg/255px-Lorne.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Lorne.jpg/340px-Lorne.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Lorne.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/John_Campbell,_9th_Duke_of_Argyll" title="John Campbell, 9th Duke of Argyll">The Marquess of Lorne</a>, Louise's husband</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Wedding_dress_of_Princess_Louise,_Duchess_of_Argyll" title="Wedding dress of Princess Louise, Duchess of Argyll">Wedding dress of Princess Louise, Duchess of Argyll</a></div>
<p>Louise became engaged to the <a href="/wiki/John_Campbell,_9th_Duke_of_Argyll" title="John Campbell, 9th Duke of Argyll">Marquess of Lorne</a> on 3 October 1870.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-London_Gazette_25_October_1870_2-1"><a href="#cite_note-London_Gazette_25_October_1870-2">[2]</a></sup> Lorne was invited to <a href="/wiki/Balmoral_Castle" title="Balmoral Castle">Balmoral Castle</a> in <a href="/wiki/Scotland" title="Scotland">Scotland</a>, and accompanied Louise, the <a href="/wiki/Lord_Chancellor" title="Lord Chancellor">Lord Chancellor</a>, <a href="/wiki/William_Wood,_1st_Baron_Hatherley" title="William Wood, 1st Baron Hatherley">Lord Hatherley</a> and Queen Victoria's <a href="/wiki/Lady-in-waiting" title="Lady-in-waiting">lady-in-waiting</a>, Jane, <a href="/wiki/Marquess_of_Ely" title="Marquess of Ely">Marchioness of Ely</a> on a drive. Later that day, Louise returned and announced to the Queen that Lorne had "spoken of his devotion" to Louise, and she accepted his proposal in the knowledge of the Queen's approval.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVictoria.2C_Queen_.28More_leaves.2974_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVictoria.2C_Queen_.28More_leaves.2974-26">[26]</a></sup> The Queen later gave Lady Ely a bracelet to mark the occasion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Queen found it difficult to let go of her daughter, confiding in her journal that she "felt painfully the thought of losing her".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVictoria.2C_Queen_.28More_leaves.2974_26-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVictoria.2C_Queen_.28More_leaves.2974-26">[26]</a></sup> The new breach in royal tradition caused surprise, especially in Germany, and Queen Victoria wrote to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Augusta_of_Saxe-Weimar" title="Augusta of Saxe-Weimar">Queen of Prussia</a> that princes of small impoverished German houses were "very unpopular" in Britain and that Lord Lorne, a "person of distinction at home" with "an independent fortune" was "really no lower in rank than minor German Royalty".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup></p>
<p>Victoria settled an annuity on Louise shortly before her marriage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-London_Gazette_3_March_1871_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-London_Gazette_3_March_1871-29">[29]</a></sup> The ceremony was conducted at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St_George%27s_Chapel_at_Windsor_Castle" title="St George's Chapel at Windsor Castle">St George's Chapel at Windsor Castle</a> on 21 March 1871,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-London_Gazette_24_March_1871_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-London_Gazette_24_March_1871-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWake1988138_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWake1988138-30">[30]</a></sup> and the crowd outside was so large that, for the first time, policemen had to form chain barriers to keep control.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWake1988139_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWake1988139-31">[31]</a></sup> Louise wore a wedding veil of <a href="/wiki/Honiton" title="Honiton">Honiton</a> lace that she designed herself, and was escorted into the Chapel by her mother, and her two eldest brothers, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Edward_VII_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Edward VII of the United Kingdom">the Prince of Wales</a> and <a href="/wiki/Alfred,_Duke_of_Saxe-Coburg_and_Gotha" title="Alfred, Duke of Saxe-Coburg and Gotha">the Duke of Edinburgh</a>. On this occasion, the usually severe black of the Queen's mourning dress was relieved by the crimson rubies and blues of the <a href="/wiki/Order_of_the_Garter#Members" title="Order of the Garter">Garter star</a>. Following the ceremony, the Queen kissed Louise, and Lorne – now a member of the royal family, but still a subject – kissed the Queen's hand.</p>
<p>The couple then journeyed to <a href="/wiki/Claremont_(country_house)" title="Claremont (country house)">Claremont</a> in <a href="/wiki/Surrey" title="Surrey">Surrey</a> for the honeymoon, but the presence of attendants on the journey, and at meal times, made it impossible for them to talk privately.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWake1988145_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWake1988145-32">[32]</a></sup> The short four-day visit did not pass without an interruption from the Queen, who was curious about her daughter's thoughts on married life. Among their wedding gifts was a maplewood desk from Queen Victoria, now at <a href="/wiki/Inveraray_Castle" title="Inveraray Castle">Inveraray Castle</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Viceregal_Consort_of_Canada">Viceregal Consort of Canada</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Princess_Louise,_Duchess_of_Argyll&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Viceregal Consort of Canada">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Inauspicious_arrival">Inauspicious arrival</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Princess_Louise,_Duchess_of_Argyll&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Inauspicious arrival">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 1878, <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Prime Minister of the United Kingdom">British Prime Minister</a>, <a href="/wiki/Benjamin_Disraeli" title="Benjamin Disraeli">Benjamin Disraeli</a>, chose Lorne to be Canada's new <a href="/wiki/Governor_General_of_Canada" title="Governor General of Canada">Governor General</a>, and he was duly appointed by Queen Victoria.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-London_Gazette_15_October_1878_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-London_Gazette_15_October_1878-34">[34]</a></sup> Louise thus became his <a href="/wiki/Viceregal_consort_of_Canada" title="Viceregal consort of Canada">Viceregal Consort</a>. On 15 November 1878, the couple left <a href="/wiki/Liverpool" title="Liverpool">Liverpool</a> and arrived for the inauguration at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Halifax_(former_city)" title="Halifax (former city)">Halifax</a> on 25 November.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWaite2000_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWaite2000-35">[35]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Princess_Louise_in_Canada.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="473" height="216" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Princess_Louise_in_Canada.jpg/170px-Princess_Louise_in_Canada.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Princess_Louise_in_Canada.jpg/255px-Princess_Louise_in_Canada.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Princess_Louise_in_Canada.jpg/340px-Princess_Louise_in_Canada.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Princess_Louise_in_Canada.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Princess Louise in Canada</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Louise became the first royal to take up residence in <a href="/wiki/Rideau_Hall" title="Rideau Hall">Rideau Hall</a>, officially the Queen's royal residence in <a href="/wiki/Ottawa" title="Ottawa">Ottawa</a>. However, the hall was far from the splendour of British royal residences, and, as each viceregal couple decorated the hall with their own furnishings, and thus took them when they departed, the Lornes found the palace sparse in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/D%C3%A9cor" title="Décor">décor</a> upon their arrival. Louise put her artistic talents to work and hung many of her watercolour and oil paintings around the hall, also installing her sculpted works. Though the news that a daughter of the Queen would be viceregal consort of Canada first saw a "thrill of joy burst upon the Dominion", it being felt that the Princess would be a strong link between Canadians and their sovereign,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESandwell200648_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESandwell200648-36">[36]</a></sup> the arrival of the new governor general and his wife was not initially welcomed by the Canadian press, which complained about the imposition of royalty on the country's hitherto un-regal society.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELongford199145_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELongford199145-37">[37]</a></sup></p>
<p>Relations with the press further deteriorated when Lorne's private secretary, <a href="/wiki/Francis_de_Winton" title="Francis de Winton">Francis de Winton</a>, threw four journalists off the royal train. Although the Lornes had no knowledge of de Winton's action, it was assumed by the press that they did, and they earned an early reputation for haughtiness.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELongford199144_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELongford199144-38">[38]</a></sup> Louise was horrified by the negative press, and when she heard about reports of "a nation of flunkies" at the viceregal court, taking lessons in "the backward walk," Louise declared that she "wouldn't care if they came in blanket coats!".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> (A reference to the ubiquitous <i><a href="/wiki/Capote_(garment)" title="Capote (garment)">capote</a></i>, a coat made of blanket-cloth, both durable and warm. The cultural significance of the blanket coat in genteel society, with reference to several early Governors-General and their wives, can be found in "'Very Picturesque and Very Canadian': The Blanket Coat and Anglo-Canadian Identity in the Second Half of the Nineteenth Century" by Eileen Stack of the <a href="/wiki/McCord_Museum" title="McCord Museum">McCord Museum</a> of Canadian History.) Eventually the worries of a rigid court at Rideau Hall and the "feeble undercurrent of criticism" turned out to be unfounded as the royal couple proved to be more relaxed than their predecessors.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHubbard1977125_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHubbard1977125-40">[40]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Canadian_entertainments">Canadian entertainments</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Princess_Louise,_Duchess_of_Argyll&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Canadian entertainments">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Toboganning_at_Government_House_in_the_time_of_Princess_Louise_c_1878.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="463" data-file-width="660" height="154" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Toboganning_at_Government_House_in_the_time_of_Princess_Louise_c_1878.JPG/220px-Toboganning_at_Government_House_in_the_time_of_Princess_Louise_c_1878.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Toboganning_at_Government_House_in_the_time_of_Princess_Louise_c_1878.JPG/330px-Toboganning_at_Government_House_in_the_time_of_Princess_Louise_c_1878.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Toboganning_at_Government_House_in_the_time_of_Princess_Louise_c_1878.JPG/440px-Toboganning_at_Government_House_in_the_time_of_Princess_Louise_c_1878.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Toboganning_at_Government_House_in_the_time_of_Princess_Louise_c_1878.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Toboganning at Government House in the time of Princess Louise, 1878 to 1883</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Louise's first few months in Canada were tinged with sadness as her favourite sister, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alice_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Alice of the United Kingdom">The Grand Duchess of Hesse and by Rhine</a>, died on 14 December 1878. Although homesick over that first Christmas, Louise soon grew accustomed to the winter climate. Sleighing and skating were two of her favourite pastimes. In Canada, as the monarch's direct representative, Lorne always took precedence over his wife, so that at the <a href="/wiki/Opening_of_the_Canadian_parliament" title="Opening of the Canadian parliament">Opening of the Parliament of Canada</a> on 13 February 1879, Louise was ranked no differently from others in attendance. She had to remain standing with the MPs, until Lorne asked them to be seated.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWake1988226_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWake1988226-41">[41]</a></sup> In order for Lorne to meet every Canadian member of Parliament, he held bi-weekly dinners for 50 people. However, some of the Canadian ladies responded negatively to the British party. One of her ladies-in-waiting reported that some had an "'I'm as good as you' sort of manner when one begins a conversation."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWake1988227_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWake1988227-42">[42]</a></sup> Court entertainments were open; anyone who could afford the clothing to attend functions was simply asked to sign the visitor's book.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWake1988228_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWake1988228-43">[43]</a></sup> Louise's first state ball was given on 19 February 1879, and she made a good impression on her guests when she ordered the silk cordon, separating the viceregal party from the guests, be removed. However, the ball was marred by various mishaps, including a drunken bandsman nearly starting a fire by pulling a curtain over a gas lamp.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWake1988228_43-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWake1988228-43">[43]</a></sup> The open house practice was criticised by guests who complained about the low social status of other guests. One attendee was horrified to find the attendee's grocer dancing in the same set.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWake1988228_43-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWake1988228-43">[43]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Opening_of_Canadian_Parliament_1879.gif"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="427" data-file-width="550" height="171" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Opening_of_Canadian_Parliament_1879.gif/220px-Opening_of_Canadian_Parliament_1879.gif" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Opening_of_Canadian_Parliament_1879.gif/330px-Opening_of_Canadian_Parliament_1879.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Opening_of_Canadian_Parliament_1879.gif/440px-Opening_of_Canadian_Parliament_1879.gif 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Opening_of_Canadian_Parliament_1879.gif" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Marquess of Lorne, accompanied by Princess Louise, opening the Canadian Parliament in 1879</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Louise and Lorne founded the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Canadian_Academy_of_Arts" title="Royal Canadian Academy of Arts">Royal Canadian Academy of Arts</a>, and enjoyed visiting <a href="/wiki/Quebec" title="Quebec">Quebec</a> (where they made their summer home), and <a href="/wiki/Toronto" title="Toronto">Toronto</a>. Louise served as patroness of the Ladies' Educational Association, of the Woman's Protective Immigration Society, of the Society of Decorative Arts and of the Art Association, all of Montreal. One of her works as a sculptor is the statue of her Royal mother <a href="/wiki/Queen_Victoria" title="Queen Victoria">Queen Victoria</a>, which now stands in front of the Royal Victoria College, Montreal,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMorgan19031_1-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMorgan19031-1">[1]</a></sup> now the <a class="external text" href="http://cac.mcgill.ca/campus/buildings/Royal_Victoria_College_Later_Years.html" rel="nofollow">Strathcona Music Building of McGill University</a>. Lorne's father, <a href="/wiki/George_Campbell,_8th_Duke_of_Argyll" title="George Campbell, 8th Duke of Argyll">The Duke of Argyll</a>, arrived with two of his daughters in June, and in the presence of the family, Louise caught a 28-pound (almost 13 kg) <a href="/wiki/Salmon" title="Salmon">salmon</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWake1988230_44-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWake1988230-44">[44]</a></sup> The women's success at fishing prompted the Duke to remark that fishing in Canada required no skill.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWake1988230_44-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWake1988230-44">[44]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sleigh_accident">Sleigh accident</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Princess_Louise,_Duchess_of_Argyll&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Sleigh accident">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:The_arrival_of_Princess_Louise_in_Hamilton,_Bermuda,_in_1883.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="564" data-file-width="857" height="145" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/The_arrival_of_Princess_Louise_in_Hamilton%2C_Bermuda%2C_in_1883.jpg/220px-The_arrival_of_Princess_Louise_in_Hamilton%2C_Bermuda%2C_in_1883.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/The_arrival_of_Princess_Louise_in_Hamilton%2C_Bermuda%2C_in_1883.jpg/330px-The_arrival_of_Princess_Louise_in_Hamilton%2C_Bermuda%2C_in_1883.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/The_arrival_of_Princess_Louise_in_Hamilton%2C_Bermuda%2C_in_1883.jpg/440px-The_arrival_of_Princess_Louise_in_Hamilton%2C_Bermuda%2C_in_1883.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:The_arrival_of_Princess_Louise_in_Hamilton,_Bermuda,_in_1883.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The arrival of Princess Louise in <a href="/wiki/Hamilton,_Bermuda" title="Hamilton, Bermuda">Hamilton, Bermuda</a> (1883)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Louise, Lorne, and two attendants, were hurt in a sleigh accident on 14 February 1880.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWake1988236_45-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWake1988236-45">[45]</a></sup> The winter was particularly severe, and the carriage in which they were traveling overturned, throwing the coachman and footman from the sleigh. The horses then panicked, and dragged the overturned carriage over more than 400 yards (370 m) of ground. Louise was knocked unconscious when she hit her head on the iron bar supporting the roof, and Lorne was trapped underneath her, expecting "the sides of the carriage to give way at any moment".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mail_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-Mail-47">[47]</a></sup> Eventually, as they overtook the sleigh ahead, the horses calmed, and the occupant of that sleigh, Princess Louise's <a href="/wiki/Aide-de-camp" title="Aide-de-camp">aide-de-camp</a>, ordered an empty carriage to convey the injured party back to <a href="/wiki/Rideau_Hall" title="Rideau Hall">Rideau Hall</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWake1988237_48-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWake1988237-48">[48]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:The_Princess_Hotel_in_Pembroke_Bermuda_on_17_July_2006.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="800" height="195" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/The_Princess_Hotel_in_Pembroke_Bermuda_on_17_July_2006.jpg/260px-The_Princess_Hotel_in_Pembroke_Bermuda_on_17_July_2006.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/The_Princess_Hotel_in_Pembroke_Bermuda_on_17_July_2006.jpg/390px-The_Princess_Hotel_in_Pembroke_Bermuda_on_17_July_2006.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/The_Princess_Hotel_in_Pembroke_Bermuda_on_17_July_2006.jpg/520px-The_Princess_Hotel_in_Pembroke_Bermuda_on_17_July_2006.jpg 2x" width="260"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:The_Princess_Hotel_in_Pembroke_Bermuda_on_17_July_2006.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Princess Hotel, in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pembroke,_Bermuda" title="Pembroke, Bermuda">Pembroke, Bermuda</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The doctors who attended Louise reported she was severely concussed and in shock, and that "it was a wonder her skull was not fractured".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWake1988237_48-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWake1988237-48">[48]</a></sup> Louise's ear had been injured when her earring caught on the side of the sleigh, tearing her <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ear_lobe" title="Ear lobe">ear lobe</a> in two.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWake1988237_48-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWake1988237-48">[48]</a></sup> The press played down the story on instructions from Lorne's private secretary, an act that was described by contemporaries as "stupid and ill advised".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWake1988238_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWake1988238-49">[49]</a></sup> For example, one New Zealand newspaper reported, "Excepting immediately after the blow, the Princess was perfectly sensible during the whole time..."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mail_47-1"><a href="#cite_note-Mail-47">[47]</a></sup> Knowledge of Louise's true condition might have elicited sympathy from the Canadian people. As it was, one <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Member_of_Parliament" title="Member of Parliament">Member of Parliament</a> wrote: "Except the cut in the lower part of the ear I think there was no injury done worth mentioning."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWake1988238_49-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWake1988238-49">[49]</a></sup> Therefore, when Louise cancelled her immediate engagements, people thought she was <a href="/wiki/Malingering" title="Malingering">malingering</a>. News of the accident was also played down in Britain, and in letters home to the anxious Queen Victoria.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWake1988238_49-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWake1988238-49">[49]</a></sup></p>
<p>She played a major role in the development of the nascent tourism industry of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/British_Overseas_Territory" title="British Overseas Territory">colony</a> of <a href="/wiki/Bermuda" title="Bermuda">Bermuda</a>, 770 miles South-east of Nova Scotia. In 1883, for reasons of her fragile health, she spent the winter in Bermuda, popularising a trend for wealthy North Americans to escape to Bermuda's relatively mild climate during the winter months. Her visit brought such attention to Bermuda that a palatial hotel, which opened in 1885, intended to cater to these new visitors, was named after her; <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Fairmont_Hamilton_Princess" title="The Fairmont Hamilton Princess">the Princess Hotel</a> was built on the shore of <a href="/wiki/Hamilton_Harbour,_Bermuda" title="Hamilton Harbour, Bermuda">Hamilton Harbour</a>, in the parish of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pembroke,_Bermuda" title="Pembroke, Bermuda">Pembroke</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Continued_interest_in_Canada">Continued interest in Canada</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Princess_Louise,_Duchess_of_Argyll&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Continued interest in Canada">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>After returning to Britain in 1883, Louise continued to take an interest in Canada. During the <a href="/wiki/North-West_Rebellion" title="North-West Rebellion">North-West Rebellion</a> of 1885 she sent a certain Dr. Boyd with medical supplies and a large fund of money for distribution. Her express instructions were that assistance was to be rendered to friend and foe indiscriminately. To fulfill her wishes, Boyd accompanied the Militia Medical Staff, under <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sir_Thomas_Roddick" title="Sir Thomas Roddick">Dr. Thomas Roddick</a> to the sites of the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Fish_Creek" title="Battle of Fish Creek">Battle of Fish Creek</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Batoche" title="Battle of Batoche">Battle of Batoche</a> to help give medical treatment to the wounded, including the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/M%C3%A9tis_people_(Canada)" title="Métis people (Canada)">Métis</a> opposition.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMacDermot193871.2C_75_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMacDermot193871.2C_75-56">[56]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1905, the province of <a href="/wiki/Alberta" title="Alberta">Alberta</a> was named after Princess Louise Caroline Alberta. In the province, there is <a href="/wiki/Lake_Louise_(Alberta)" title="Lake Louise (Alberta)">Lake Louise</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Mount_Alberta" title="Mount Alberta">Mount Alberta</a> is named in her honour.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PlaceNames_58-0"><a href="#cite_note-PlaceNames-58">[58]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Victoria.27s_last_years">Victoria's last years</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Princess_Louise,_Duchess_of_Argyll&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Victoria's last years">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Family_conflict">Family conflict</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Princess_Louise,_Duchess_of_Argyll&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Family conflict">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="vertical-navbox" style="float:right;clear:right;width:22.0em;margin:0 0 1.0em 1.0em;background:#f9f9f9;border:1px solid #aaa;padding:0.2em;border-spacing:0.4em 0;text-align:center;line-height:1.4em;font-size:88%;background: #FFFFFF; border-collapse:collapse;">
<tr>
<td style="padding-top:0.4em;line-height:1.2em"><a href="/wiki/Monarchy_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Monarchy of the United Kingdom">British Royalty</a></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th style="padding:0.2em 0.4em 0.2em;padding-top:0;font-size:145%;line-height:1.2em"><a href="/wiki/House_of_Saxe-Coburg_and_Gotha" title="House of Saxe-Coburg and Gotha">House of Saxe-Coburg and Gotha</a></th>
</tr>
<tr>
<td style="padding:0.2em 0 0.4em"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Coat_of_Arms_of_the_United_Kingdom_(1837-1952).svg"><img alt="Coat of Arms of the United Kingdom (1837-1952).svg" data-file-height="1550" data-file-width="1550" height="160" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Coat_of_Arms_of_the_United_Kingdom_%281837-1952%29.svg/160px-Coat_of_Arms_of_the_United_Kingdom_%281837-1952%29.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Coat_of_Arms_of_the_United_Kingdom_%281837-1952%29.svg/240px-Coat_of_Arms_of_the_United_Kingdom_%281837-1952%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Coat_of_Arms_of_the_United_Kingdom_%281837-1952%29.svg/320px-Coat_of_Arms_of_the_United_Kingdom_%281837-1952%29.svg.png 2x" width="160"/></a></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th style="padding:0.1em;background: #C5C5DD; border-top: 1px solid #AAA; border-bottom: 1px solid #AAA; padding: 0.3em 0.5em; text-align: left;"><a href="/wiki/Queen_Victoria" title="Queen Victoria">Victoria</a> and <a href="/wiki/Albert,_Prince_Consort" title="Albert, Prince Consort">Albert</a></th>
</tr>
<tr>
<td style="padding:0 0.1em 0.4em;text-align: left; padding:0.3em 0.5em;">

<dd><a href="/wiki/Victoria,_Princess_Royal" title="Victoria, Princess Royal">Victoria, Princess Royal and German Empress</a></dd>

<dd><a href="/wiki/Princess_Alice_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Princess Alice of the United Kingdom">Alice, Grand Duchess of Hesse and by Rhine</a></dd>

<dd><a href="/wiki/Princess_Helena_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Princess Helena of the United Kingdom">Helena, Princess Christian of Schleswig-Holstein</a></dd>

<tr>
<td style="text-align:right;font-size:115%;padding-right: 0.5em;">
