<ul>
<li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:House_of_Saxe-Coburg_and_Gotha_(UK)" title="Template:House of Saxe-Coburg and Gotha (UK)"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li>
<li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:House_of_Saxe-Coburg_and_Gotha_(UK)" title="Template talk:House of Saxe-Coburg and Gotha (UK)"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li>
<li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:House_of_Saxe-Coburg_and_Gotha_(UK)&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li>
</ul>
</div>
</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>Louise returned to Britain, from <a href="/wiki/Quebec" title="Quebec">Quebec</a>, with her husband on 27 October 1883, and landed at <a href="/wiki/Liverpool" title="Liverpool">Liverpool</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWake1988264_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWake1988264-59">[59]</a></sup> Queen Victoria had prepared apartments at <a href="/wiki/Kensington_Palace" title="Kensington Palace">Kensington Palace</a>, and the couple took up official residence there. Louise retained those apartments until her death there 56 years later. Lorne resumed his political career, campaigning unsuccessfully for the <a href="/wiki/Hampstead_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Hampstead (UK Parliament constituency)">Hampstead</a> seat in 1885. In 1896, he won the <a href="/wiki/Manchester_South_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Manchester South (UK Parliament constituency)">South Manchester</a> seat, entering parliament as a <a href="/wiki/Liberal_Party_(UK)" title="Liberal Party (UK)">Liberal</a>. Louise, unlike Lorne and his father, was in favour of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Irish_Home_Rule" title="Irish Home Rule">Irish Home Rule</a>, and disappointed when he <a href="/wiki/Defection" title="Defection">defected</a> from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gladstonian_Liberalism" title="Gladstonian Liberalism">Gladstonian Liberalism</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Liberal_Unionist_Party" title="Liberal Unionist Party">Liberal Unionists</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWake1988282_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWake1988282-60">[60]</a></sup> Relations between Louise and Lorne were strained, and, despite the Queen's attempts to keep them under one roof, they often went their separate ways.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWake1988270_61-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWake1988270-61">[61]</a></sup> Even when he accompanied Louise, he was not always received with favour at court, and the Prince of Wales did not take to him.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcDougall_1988.2C_Later_years_.281883.E2.80.931939.29_62-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcDougall_1988.2C_Later_years_.281883.E2.80.931939.29-62">[62]</a></sup> Out of all the royal family, Lorne was the only one to be identified closely with a political party, having been a <a href="/wiki/Gladstonian_liberalism" title="Gladstonian liberalism">Gladstonian</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Liberal_party_(UK)" title="Liberal party (UK)">liberal</a> in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/British_House_of_Commons" title="British House of Commons">House of Commons</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWaite2000_35-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWaite2000-35">[35]</a></sup></p>
<p>Louise's relationship with the two sisters closest to the Queen, <a href="/wiki/Princess_Beatrice_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Princess Beatrice of the United Kingdom">Beatrice</a> and <a href="/wiki/Princess_Helena_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Princess Helena of the United Kingdom">Helena</a>, was strained at best. Beatrice had married the tall and handsome <a href="/wiki/Prince_Henry_of_Battenberg" title="Prince Henry of Battenberg">Prince Henry of Battenberg</a> in a love match in 1885, and they had four children. Louise, who had a jealous nature, had grown accustomed to treating Beatrice with pity on account of the Queen's constant need for her.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDennison2007198_63-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDennison2007198-63">[63]</a></sup> Beatrice's biographer, Matthew Dennison, claims that in contrast to Beatrice, Louise remained strikingly good looking throughout her forties.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDennison2007199_64-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDennison2007199-64">[64]</a></sup> Louise and her husband were no longer close, and rumours spread about Lorne's alleged homosexuality.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> Thus, Beatrice was enjoying a satisfying sexual relationship with her popular husband, which Louise was not.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWake1988315_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWake1988315-66">[66]</a></sup> Louise may have considered Prince Henry a more appropriate husband for herself.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDennison2007198_63-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDennison2007198-63">[63]</a></sup> Certainly, following Prince Henry's death in 1896, Louise wrote that: "he [Henry] was almost the greatest friend I had—I, too, miss him more than I can say".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDennison2007198_63-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDennison2007198-63">[63]</a></sup> In addition, Louise attempted to champion her late brother-in-law by announcing that she was his confidante and that Beatrice, a mere cipher, meant nothing to him.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELutyens196152_67-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELutyens196152-67">[67]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rumours_regarding_Louise">Rumours regarding Louise</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Princess_Louise,_Duchess_of_Argyll&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Rumours regarding Louise">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Further rumours spread that Louise was having an affair with <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Bigge,_1st_Baron_Stamfordham" title="Arthur Bigge, 1st Baron Stamfordham">Arthur Bigge</a>, later <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baron_Stamfordham" title="Baron Stamfordham">Lord Stamfordham</a>, the Queen's <a href="/wiki/Private_Secretary_to_the_Sovereign" title="Private Secretary to the Sovereign">assistant private secretary</a>. Beatrice mentioned the rumours to the Queen's physician, calling it a "scandal",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDennison2007199_64-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDennison2007199-64">[64]</a></sup> and Prince Henry claimed to have seen Bigge drinking to Louise's health at dinner.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDennison2007199_64-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDennison2007199-64">[64]</a></sup> Louise denied the rumour, claiming that it was started by Beatrice and Helena to undermine her position at court.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDennison2007201_68-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDennison2007201-68">[68]</a></sup> However, on Henry's death, relations between the sisters sporadically improved, and it was Louise, rather than the Queen, who was the first to arrive at <a href="/wiki/Cimiez" title="Cimiez">Cimiez</a> to be with the widowed Beatrice.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDennison2007200_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDennison2007200-69">[69]</a></sup> Nevertheless, Louise's jealousy did not evaporate completely. James Reid, the Queen's <a href="/wiki/Physician" title="Physician">physician</a>, wrote to his wife a few years later: "Louise is as usual much down on her sisters. Hope she won't stay long or she will do mischief!"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup></p>
<p>Rumours of affairs did not surround only Bigge. In 1890, the sculptor <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Edgar_Boehm" title="Joseph Edgar Boehm">Joseph Edgar Boehm</a> died in Louise's presence at his studio in <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a>, leading to rumours that the two were having an affair.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStocker_2004.2C_Louise.2C_Princess.2C_duchess_of_Argyll_4-6"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStocker_2004.2C_Louise.2C_Princess.2C_duchess_of_Argyll-4">[4]</a></sup> Boehm's assistant, <a href="/wiki/Alfred_Gilbert" title="Alfred Gilbert">Alfred Gilbert</a>, who played a central role in comforting Louise after Boehm's death, and supervised the destruction of Boehm's private papers,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStocker_2004.2C_.28Joseph.29_Edgar_Boehm_71-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStocker_2004.2C_.28Joseph.29_Edgar_Boehm-71">[71]</a></sup> was rapidly promoted as a royal sculptor.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStocker_2004.2C_.28Joseph.29_Edgar_Boehm_71-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStocker_2004.2C_.28Joseph.29_Edgar_Boehm-71">[71]</a></sup> Louise was also romantically linked to fellow artist <a href="/wiki/Edwin_Lutyens" title="Edwin Lutyens">Edwin Lutyens</a>; her <a href="/wiki/Equerry" title="Equerry">equerry</a>, Colonel William Probert; and an unnamed music master.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWake1988321_72-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWake1988321-72">[72]</a></sup> However, <a href="/wiki/Jehanne_Wake" title="Jehanne Wake">Jehanne Wake</a>, Louise's biographer, argues that there is no substantial evidence to suggest that Louise had sexual relationships with anyone other than her husband.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWake1988321_72-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWake1988321-72">[72]</a></sup></p>
<p>During Victoria's last years, Louise carried out a range of public duties, such as opening public buildings, laying foundation stones, and officiating at special programmes. Louise, like her eldest sister <a href="/wiki/Victoria,_Princess_Royal" title="Victoria, Princess Royal">Victoria</a>, was more liberally minded, and supported the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Suffragist" title="Suffragist">suffragist</a> movement, completely contrary to the Queen's views.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcDougall_1988.2C_Later_years_.281883.E2.80.931939.29_62-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcDougall_1988.2C_Later_years_.281883.E2.80.931939.29-62">[62]</a></sup> Louise privately visited Britain's first female doctor, <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_Garrett_Anderson" title="Elizabeth Garrett Anderson">Elizabeth Garrett</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWake198898_73-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWake198898-73">[73]</a></sup> Queen Victoria deplored the idea of women joining professions, especially the medical profession, and described the training of female doctors as a "repulsive subject".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELongford1987395_74-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELongford1987395-74">[74]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Louise_as_unconventional_royal">Louise as unconventional royal</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Princess_Louise,_Duchess_of_Argyll&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Louise as unconventional royal">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Princess_Louise_Caroline_Alberta_(Princess_Louise,_Duchess_of_Argyll).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="594" data-file-width="449" height="225" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Princess_Louise_Caroline_Alberta_%28Princess_Louise%2C_Duchess_of_Argyll%29.jpg/170px-Princess_Louise_Caroline_Alberta_%28Princess_Louise%2C_Duchess_of_Argyll%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Princess_Louise_Caroline_Alberta_%28Princess_Louise%2C_Duchess_of_Argyll%29.jpg/255px-Princess_Louise_Caroline_Alberta_%28Princess_Louise%2C_Duchess_of_Argyll%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Princess_Louise_Caroline_Alberta_%28Princess_Louise%2C_Duchess_of_Argyll%29.jpg/340px-Princess_Louise_Caroline_Alberta_%28Princess_Louise%2C_Duchess_of_Argyll%29.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Princess_Louise_Caroline_Alberta_(Princess_Louise,_Duchess_of_Argyll).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Princess Louise, Duchess of Argyll c. 1900 by <a href="/wiki/William_James_Topley" title="William James Topley">William James Topley</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Louise was determined to be seen as an ordinary person and not as a member of the court. When travelling abroad, she often used the alias "Mrs Campbell".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcDougall_1988.2C_Later_years_.281883.E2.80.931939.29_62-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcDougall_1988.2C_Later_years_.281883.E2.80.931939.29-62">[62]</a></sup> Louise was known for her charity towards servants. On one occasion, the butler approached her and requested permission to dismiss the second footman, who was late getting out of bed. When she advised that the footman be given an alarm clock, the butler informed her that he already had one. She then went so far as to suggest a bed that would throw him out at a specified time, but she was told this was not feasible. Finally, she suggested that he might be ill, and when checked, he was found to be suffering from <a href="/wiki/Tuberculosis" title="Tuberculosis">tuberculosis</a>. The footman was therefore sent to <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a> to recover.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcDougall_1988.2C_Later_years_.281883.E2.80.931939.29_62-3"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcDougall_1988.2C_Later_years_.281883.E2.80.931939.29-62">[62]</a></sup></p>
<p>On another occasion, when she visited <a href="/wiki/Bermuda" title="Bermuda">Bermuda</a>, she was invited to a reception and chose to walk rather than be driven. She became thirsty along the way and stopped at a house, where she asked a black woman named Mrs McCarthy for a glass of water. Owing to the scarcity of water, the woman had to go some distance to obtain it, but was reluctant because she had to finish her ironing. When Louise offered to continue the ironing, the woman refused, adding that she was in a great hurry to finish so that she could go and see Princess Louise. Realising that she had not been recognised, Louise enquired whether McCarthy would recognise her again. When the woman said that she would have thought so, but was admittedly unsure, Louise replied: "Well take a good look at me now, so you can be sure to know me tomorrow at St. Georges."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWake1988258.E2.80.93259_75-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWake1988258.E2.80.93259-75">[75]</a></sup> The Princess clung to her privacy, and enjoyed not being recognised.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWake1988259_76-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWake1988259-76">[76]</a></sup></p>
<p>Louise and her sisters had another disagreement after the death of the Queen's close friend, <a href="/wiki/Jane_Spencer,_Baroness_Churchill" title="Jane Spencer, Baroness Churchill">Jane Spencer, Baroness Churchill</a>. Determined not to put her mother through more misery, Louise wanted the news to be broken to the Queen gradually. When this was not done, Louise voiced her sharp criticism of Helena and Beatrice.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELongford199170_77-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELongford199170-77">[77]</a></sup> One month later, on 22 January 1901, Queen Victoria died at <a href="/wiki/Osborne_House" title="Osborne House">Osborne House</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Isle_of_Wight" title="Isle of Wight">Isle of Wight</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELongford1987561.E2.80.93562_78-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELongford1987561.E2.80.93562-78">[78]</a></sup> In her will, the Queen bequeathed Kent House, on the Osborne Estate, to Louise as a country residence,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDennison2007226_79-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDennison2007226-79">[79]</a></sup> and gave Osborne Cottage to Louise's youngest sister, Beatrice. Louise and Beatrice were now neighbours both at Kensington Palace and Osborne.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWake1988346_80-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWake1988346-80">[80]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Later_life">Later life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Princess_Louise,_Duchess_of_Argyll&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Later life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Edwardian_period">Edwardian period</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Princess_Louise,_Duchess_of_Argyll&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Edwardian period">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Upon Queen Victoria's death, Louise entered the social circle of her brother, the new <a href="/wiki/Edward_VII" title="Edward VII">King Edward VII</a>, with whom she had much in common, including smoking.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELongford199174_81-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELongford199174-81">[81]</a></sup> She had an obsession with physical fitness, and if she was sneered at for this, she would retort by saying: "Never mind, I'll outlive you all."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> Meanwhile, Louise's husband, 9th Duke of Argyll since 1900, took his seat in the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Lords" title="House of Lords">House of Lords</a>. The Colonial Secretary, <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Chamberlain" title="Joseph Chamberlain">Joseph Chamberlain</a>, offered him the office of <a href="/wiki/Governor-General_of_Australia" title="Governor-General of Australia">Governor-General of Australia</a> that year, but the offer was declined.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWaite2000_35-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWaite2000-35">[35]</a></sup> Louise continued her sculpture, and in 1902, designed a memorial to the colonial soldiers who died in the <a href="/wiki/Second_Boer_War" title="Second Boer War">Boer War</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELongford199173_83-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELongford199173-83">[83]</a></sup> In the same year, she began a nude study on a married woman suggested by the English painter Sir <a href="/wiki/William_Blake_Richmond" title="William Blake Richmond">William Blake Richmond</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELongford199173_83-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELongford199173-83">[83]</a></sup></p>
<p>Louise spent much of her time at Kent House, and she frequently visited Scotland with her husband. Financial pressures did not disappear when Lorne became Duke, and Louise avoided inviting the King to <a href="/wiki/Inveraray" title="Inveraray">Inveraray</a>, Argyll's ancestral home, because the couple were economising. When Queen Victoria had visited the house before Lorne became Duke of Argyll, there were seventy servants and seventy-four dogs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELongford199174_81-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELongford199174-81">[81]</a></sup> By the time of Edward VII's accession, there were four servants and two dogs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELongford199174_81-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELongford199174-81">[81]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Duke of Argyll's health continued to deteriorate. He became increasingly <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Senile" title="Senile">senile</a>, and Louise nursed him devotedly from 1911. In these years Louise and her husband were closer than they had been before.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStocker_2004.2C_Louise.2C_Princess.2C_duchess_of_Argyll_4-7"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStocker_2004.2C_Louise.2C_Princess.2C_duchess_of_Argyll-4">[4]</a></sup> In spring 1914 Louise stayed at <a href="/wiki/Kensington_Palace" title="Kensington Palace">Kensington Palace</a> while her husband remained on the <a href="/wiki/Isle_of_Wight" title="Isle of Wight">Isle of Wight</a>.</p>
<p>He developed bronchial problems followed by double <a href="/wiki/Pneumonia" title="Pneumonia">pneumonia</a>. Louise was summoned on 28 April 1914, and he died on 2 May.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELongford199177_84-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELongford199177-84">[84]</a></sup> Following his death, Louise had a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nervous_breakdown" title="Nervous breakdown">nervous breakdown</a> and suffered from intense loneliness, writing to a friend shortly afterwards: "My loneliness without the Duke is quite terrible. I wonder what he does now!"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Last_years">Last years</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Princess_Louise,_Duchess_of_Argyll&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Last years">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Louise spent her last years at <a href="/wiki/Kensington_Palace" title="Kensington Palace">Kensington Palace</a>, occupying rooms next to her sister <a href="/wiki/Princess_Beatrice_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Princess Beatrice of the United Kingdom">Princess Beatrice</a>. She made occasional public appearances with the royal family, such as at the <a href="/wiki/Cenotaph#The_Cenotaph.2C_London" title="Cenotaph">Cenotaph</a> at <a href="/wiki/Whitehall" title="Whitehall">Whitehall</a> on 11 November 1925. However, her health deteriorated. In 1935, she greeted her nephew, <a href="/wiki/George_V" title="George V">King George V</a>, and his wife, <a href="/wiki/Mary_of_Teck" title="Mary of Teck">Queen Mary</a>, at Kensington Town Hall during their Silver Jubilee celebrations, and was made an Honorary Freeman of the Borough of Kensington. Her last public appearance occurred in 1937, at the Home Arts and Industries Exhibition. Between these occasions, her great nephew, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/King_Edward_VIII" title="King Edward VIII">King Edward VIII</a>, abdicated on 11 December 1936. In December 1936, Louise wrote to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/British_prime_minister" title="British prime minister">British prime minister</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stanley_Baldwin" title="Stanley Baldwin">Stanley Baldwin</a>, sympathising with him about the <a href="/wiki/Edward_VIII_abdication_crisis" title="Edward VIII abdication crisis">crisis</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELongford1991306_86-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELongford1991306-86">[86]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Princess_Louise%27s_grave_at_Frogmore.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="430" data-file-width="809" height="117" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Princess_Louise%27s_grave_at_Frogmore.jpg/220px-Princess_Louise%27s_grave_at_Frogmore.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Princess_Louise%27s_grave_at_Frogmore.jpg/330px-Princess_Louise%27s_grave_at_Frogmore.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Princess_Louise%27s_grave_at_Frogmore.jpg/440px-Princess_Louise%27s_grave_at_Frogmore.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Princess_Louise%27s_grave_at_Frogmore.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Princess Louise's grave (centre) at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Royal_Burial_Ground" title="Royal Burial Ground">Royal Burial Ground</a> at <a href="/wiki/Frogmore" title="Frogmore">Frogmore</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Following the accession of Edward's brother <a href="/wiki/George_VI" title="George VI">King George VI</a>, she became too ill to move around, and was confined to Kensington Palace, affectionately called the "Auntie Palace" by <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II" title="Elizabeth II">Princess Elizabeth</a> and <a href="/wiki/Princess_Margaret,_Countess_of_Snowdon" title="Princess Margaret, Countess of Snowdon">Princess Margaret</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELongford199180_87-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELongford199180-87">[87]</a></sup> She developed <a href="/wiki/Neuritis" title="Neuritis">neuritis</a> in her arm, inflammation of the nerves between the ribs, fainting fits, and <a href="/wiki/Sciatica" title="Sciatica">sciatica</a>. Louise occupied herself by drafting prayers, one of which was sent to <a href="/wiki/Neville_Chamberlain" title="Neville Chamberlain">Neville Chamberlain</a>, reading "Guide our Ministers of State and all who are in authority over us ... "<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELongford199181_88-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELongford199181-88">[88]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Death">Death</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Princess_Louise,_Duchess_of_Argyll&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Death">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>She died at Kensington Palace on the morning of 3 December 1939 at the age of 91 years, 8 months and 15 days, the same age to the day as her younger brother Prince Arthur,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-London_Gazette_1_December_1939_89-0"><a href="#cite_note-London_Gazette_1_December_1939-89">[89]</a></sup> wearing the wedding veil she had worn almost 70 years earlier.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWake1988413_90-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWake1988413-90">[90]</a></sup> Following a simple funeral, owing to the war, her remains were <a href="/wiki/Cremation" title="Cremation">cremated</a> at <a href="/wiki/Golders_Green_Crematorium" title="Golders Green Crematorium">Golders Green Crematorium</a> on 8 December.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWake1988412_91-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWake1988412-91">[91]</a></sup> Her ashes were quietly placed in the Royal Crypt at St. George's Chapel on 12 December, with many members of the Royal and Argyll families present.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWake1988412_91-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWake1988412-91">[91]</a></sup> Her ashes were moved to the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Burial_Ground,_Frogmore" title="Royal Burial Ground, Frogmore">Royal Burial Ground, Frogmore</a> near Windsor, on 13 March 1940.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELongford199183_92-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELongford199183-92">[92]</a></sup> Louise's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Will_(law)" title="Will (law)">will</a> stated that if she died in <a href="/wiki/Scotland" title="Scotland">Scotland</a> she should be buried at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Campbell_mausoleum" title="Campbell mausoleum">Campbell mausoleum</a> in <a href="/wiki/Kilmun" title="Kilmun">Kilmun</a> next to her husband; if in England, at <a href="/wiki/Frogmore" title="Frogmore">Frogmore</a> near her parents.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWake1988412_91-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWake1988412-91">[91]</a></sup> Her coffin was borne by eight NCOs of her own regiment, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Argyll_and_Sutherland_Highlanders_(Princess_Louise%27s)" title="The Argyll and Sutherland Highlanders (Princess Louise's)">The Argyll and Sutherland Highlanders</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Legacy">Legacy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Princess_Louise,_Duchess_of_Argyll&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Legacy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Victoria_statue_Kensington.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="743" data-file-width="1024" height="160" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Victoria_statue_Kensington.jpg/220px-Victoria_statue_Kensington.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Victoria_statue_Kensington.jpg/330px-Victoria_statue_Kensington.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Victoria_statue_Kensington.jpg/440px-Victoria_statue_Kensington.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Victoria_statue_Kensington.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Louise's statue of Queen Victoria at Kensington Palace</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Louise bestowed her name on four Canadian regiments: <a href="/wiki/The_Argyll_and_Sutherland_Highlanders_of_Canada_(Princess_Louise%27s)" title="The Argyll and Sutherland Highlanders of Canada (Princess Louise's)">The Argyll and Sutherland Highlanders of Canada (Princess Louise's)</a> in Hamilton, Ontario; the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Princess_Louise_Dragoon_Guards" title="Princess Louise Dragoon Guards">Princess Louise Dragoon Guards</a> in Ottawa, Ontario (inactive since 1965); the <a href="/wiki/8th_Canadian_Hussars_(Princess_Louise%27s)" title="8th Canadian Hussars (Princess Louise's)">8th Canadian Hussars (Princess Louise's)</a> in <a href="/wiki/Moncton" title="Moncton">Moncton</a>, New Brunswick; and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Princess_Louise_Fusiliers" title="Princess Louise Fusiliers">Princess Louise Fusiliers</a> in Halifax, Nova Scotia.</p>
<p>Queen Elizabeth II later recalled that Louise and her sister <a href="/wiki/Princess_Beatrice_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Princess Beatrice of the United Kingdom">Beatrice</a> would talk until they stunned their audience with their output of words.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWake1988410_94-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWake1988410-94">[94]</a></sup></p>
<p>The province of <a href="/wiki/Alberta" title="Alberta">Alberta</a> in <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a> is named after her. Although the name "Louise" was originally planned, the Princess wished to honour her dead father, so her last name was chosen. <a href="/wiki/Lake_Louise,_Alberta" title="Lake Louise, Alberta">Lake Louise</a> in Alberta is also named after her, as is <a href="/wiki/Mount_Alberta" title="Mount Alberta">Mount Alberta</a>. Although her time in Canada was not always happy, she liked the Canadian people and retained close links with her Canadian regiments.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStocker_2004.2C_Louise.2C_Princess.2C_duchess_of_Argyll_4-8"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStocker_2004.2C_Louise.2C_Princess.2C_duchess_of_Argyll-4">[4]</a></sup> Back at home, she gained a reputation for paying unscheduled visits to hospitals, especially during her later years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStocker_2004.2C_Louise.2C_Princess.2C_duchess_of_Argyll_4-9"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStocker_2004.2C_Louise.2C_Princess.2C_duchess_of_Argyll-4">[4]</a></sup> Her relationship with her family was generally close. Although at times she bickered with the Queen, and her sisters Helena and Beatrice, the relations did not remain strained for long. She retained a lifelong correspondence with her brother, <a href="/wiki/Prince_Arthur,_Duke_of_Connaught_and_Strathearn" title="Prince Arthur, Duke of Connaught and Strathearn">Prince Arthur</a>, and was one of King Edward VII's favourite sisters.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWake1988350_95-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWake1988350-95">[95]</a></sup> Of all her siblings, she was closest to <a href="/wiki/Prince_Leopold,_Duke_of_Albany" title="Prince Leopold, Duke of Albany">Prince Leopold</a>, later <a href="/wiki/Duke_of_Albany" title="Duke of Albany">Duke of Albany</a>, and she was devastated by his death in 1884.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWake1988269_96-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWake1988269-96">[96]</a></sup></p>
<p>Among the younger generations of the family, Louise's favourite relatives were <a href="/wiki/Prince_George,_Duke_of_Kent" title="Prince George, Duke of Kent">the Duke</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Princess_Marina,_Duchess_of_Kent" title="Princess Marina, Duchess of Kent">Duchess of Kent</a>, her grandnephew and his wife.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELongford199180_87-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELongford199180-87">[87]</a></sup> At the <a href="/wiki/Coronation_of_King_George_VI_and_Queen_Elizabeth" title="Coronation of King George VI and Queen Elizabeth">coronation of King George VI and Queen Elizabeth</a> in 1937, Louise lent the Duchess the <a href="/wiki/Train_(clothing)" title="Train (clothing)">train</a> that she designed and wore for the <a href="/wiki/Coronation_of_King_Edward_VII_and_Queen_Alexandra" title="Coronation of King Edward VII and Queen Alexandra">coronation of King Edward VII and Queen Alexandra</a> in 1902.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWake1988411_97-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWake1988411-97">[97]</a></sup></p>
<p>A war hospital in <a href="/wiki/Erskine" title="Erskine">Erskine</a>, Scotland, is named after Louise. It took her name as she was the first <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Patron" title="Patron">patron</a> of the unit. It was originally called <a href="/wiki/Erskine_(charity)" title="Erskine (charity)"><i>Princess Louise Scottish Hospital for Limbless Sailors and Soldiers</i></a>. The name changed over the years to <i>Erskine Hospital</i> and then just <i>Erskine</i>. The charity is close to its centenary year and has grown to become the biggest ex-service establishment in the country.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Art_Practice">Art Practice</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Princess_Louise,_Duchess_of_Argyll&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Art Practice">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Louise had artistic training from childhood, first with <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Susan_Durant&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Susan Durant (page does not exist)">Susan Durant</a> from 1864, then <a href="/wiki/Mary_Thornycroft" title="Mary Thornycroft">Mary Thornycroft</a> from 1867, and further lessons with <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Edgar_Boehm" title="Joseph Edgar Boehm">Edgar Boehm</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_98-0"><a href="#cite_note-:0-98">[98]</a></sup> She also then attended <a href="/wiki/Royal_College_of_Art" title="Royal College of Art">National Art Training School</a>, or NATS, which marks the first time a member of the British royal family attended a public education institution. Like many women artists in the nineteenth century, Louise had to make do with training intended for industrial designers and art teachers rather than fine artists. There was no training from the nude model, as there was for male art students.</p>
<p>Louise held an account with the London artists’ colourman Charles Roberson &amp; Co. from April 1872 until February 1931, buying materials for oil and water colour painting including numerous sketchbooks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup></p>
<p>Louise was the most artistically talented of Queen Victoria's daughters. As well as being an able actress, pianist and dancer, she was a prolific artist and sculptor. When Louise sculpted a statue of the Queen, portraying her in Coronation robes, the press claimed that her tutor, <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Edgar_Boehm" title="Joseph Edgar Boehm">Sir Edgar Boehm</a>, was the true creator of the work. The claim was denied by Louise's friends, who asserted her effort and independence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWake1988302_100-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWake1988302-100">[100]</a></sup> The work was intended to be exhibited in 1887, but production was delayed until 1893. A memorial to her brother-in-law, <a href="/wiki/Prince_Henry_of_Battenberg" title="Prince Henry of Battenberg">Prince Henry of Battenberg</a>, and a memorial to the Colonial soldiers who fell during the <a href="/wiki/Second_Boer_War" title="Second Boer War">Boer War</a>, reside at <a href="/wiki/Whippingham" title="Whippingham">Whippingham</a> Church on the <a href="/wiki/Isle_of_Wight" title="Isle of Wight">Isle of Wight</a>, and another statue of Queen Victoria remains at <a href="/wiki/McGill_University" title="McGill University">McGill University</a> in <a href="/wiki/Montreal" title="Montreal">Montreal</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStocker_2004.2C_Louise.2C_Princess.2C_duchess_of_Argyll_4-10"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStocker_2004.2C_Louise.2C_Princess.2C_duchess_of_Argyll-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Selected_Works_of_Art">Selected Works of Art</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Princess_Louise,_Duchess_of_Argyll&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Selected Works of Art">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Honours">Honours</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Princess_Louise,_Duchess_of_Argyll&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Honours">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>

<li><b>3 June 1918</b>: <a href="/wiki/Order_of_the_British_Empire" title="Order of the British Empire">Dame Grand Cross of the Order of the British Empire</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-London_Gazette_4_June_1918_107-0"><a href="#cite_note-London_Gazette_4_June_1918-107">[107]</a></sup></li>
<li><b>12 June 1927</b>: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Venerable_Order_of_Saint_John" title="Venerable Order of Saint John">Dame Grand Cross of the Venerable Order of St John</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-London_Gazette_14_June_1927_108-0"><a href="#cite_note-London_Gazette_14_June_1927-108">[108]</a></sup></li>
<li><b>11 May 1937</b>: <a href="/wiki/Royal_Victorian_Order" title="Royal Victorian Order">Dame Grand Cross of the Royal Victorian Order</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-London_Gazette_11_May_1937_109-0"><a href="#cite_note-London_Gazette_11_May_1937-109">[109]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Honorary_military_appointments">Honorary military appointments</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Princess_Louise,_Duchess_of_Argyll&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Honorary military appointments">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<ul>
<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada"><img alt="Canada" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="500" data-file-width="1000" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Canadian_Red_Ensign_1921-1957.svg/23px-Canadian_Red_Ensign_1921-1957.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Canadian_Red_Ensign_1921-1957.svg/35px-Canadian_Red_Ensign_1921-1957.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Canadian_Red_Ensign_1921-1957.svg/46px-Canadian_Red_Ensign_1921-1957.svg.png 2x" width="23"/></a></span> <b>3 July 1911</b>: Honorary Colonel, 5th Princess Louise Dragoon Guards (which became <a href="/wiki/4th_Princess_Louise_Dragoon_Guards" title="4th Princess Louise Dragoon Guards">4th Princess Louise Dragoon Guards</a> in 1936)</li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom"><img alt="United Kingdom" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="1200" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/ae/Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/ae/Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/ae/Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg/46px-Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg.png 2x" width="23"/></a></span> <b>22 June 1914</b>: Colonel-in-Chief, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Argyll_and_Sutherland_Highlanders_(Princess_Louise%27s)" title="The Argyll and Sutherland Highlanders (Princess Louise's)">the Argyll and Sutherland Highlanders (Princess Louise's)</a></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada"><img alt="Canada" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="500" data-file-width="1000" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Canadian_Red_Ensign_1921-1957.svg/23px-Canadian_Red_Ensign_1921-1957.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Canadian_Red_Ensign_1921-1957.svg/35px-Canadian_Red_Ensign_1921-1957.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Canadian_Red_Ensign_1921-1957.svg/46px-Canadian_Red_Ensign_1921-1957.svg.png 2x" width="23"/></a></span> <b>15 April 1930</b>: Colonel-in-Chief, <a href="/wiki/The_Argyll_and_Sutherland_Highlanders_of_Canada_(Princess_Louise%27s)" title="The Argyll and Sutherland Highlanders of Canada (Princess Louise's)">the Argyll and Sutherland Highlanders of Canada (Princess Louise's)</a></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada"><img alt="Canada" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="500" data-file-width="1000" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Canadian_Red_Ensign_1921-1957.svg/23px-Canadian_Red_Ensign_1921-1957.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Canadian_Red_Ensign_1921-1957.svg/35px-Canadian_Red_Ensign_1921-1957.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Canadian_Red_Ensign_1921-1957.svg/46px-Canadian_Red_Ensign_1921-1957.svg.png 2x" width="23"/></a></span> <b>14 August 1936</b>: Colonel-in-Chief, <a href="/wiki/The_Princess_Louise_Fusiliers" title="The Princess Louise Fusiliers">the Princess Louise Fusiliers</a></li>
</ul>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Honorary_roles">Honorary roles</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Princess_Louise,_Duchess_of_Argyll&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Honorary roles">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<ul>
<li>President of the Women's Education Union from 1871.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStocker_2004.2C_Louise.2C_Princess.2C_duchess_of_Argyll_4-11"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStocker_2004.2C_Louise.2C_Princess.2C_duchess_of_Argyll-4">[4]</a></sup></li>
<li>Patron of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Girls%27_Public_Day_School_Company" title="Girls' Public Day School Company">Girls' Day School Trust</a>, 1872–1939<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStocker_2004.2C_Louise.2C_Princess.2C_duchess_of_Argyll_4-12"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStocker_2004.2C_Louise.2C_Princess.2C_duchess_of_Argyll-4">[4]</a></sup></li>
<li>Patron of the Ladies Lifeboat Guild, Royal National Lifeboat Institution, 1923-39<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Arms">Arms</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Princess_Louise,_Duchess_of_Argyll&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Arms">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 1858, Louise and the three younger of her sisters were granted use of the <a href="/wiki/Royal_coat_of_arms_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Royal coat of arms of the United Kingdom">royal arms</a>, with an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Inescutcheon" title="Inescutcheon">inescutcheon</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Coat_of_arms_of_Saxony" title="Coat of arms of Saxony">shield of Saxony</a> and differenced by a <a href="/wiki/Label_(heraldry)" title="Label (heraldry)">label</a> of three points <a href="/wiki/Argent" title="Argent">argent</a>. On Louise's arms, the outer points bore cantons <a href="/wiki/Gules" title="Gules">gules</a>, and the centre a rose gules. In 1917, the inescutcheon was dropped by royal warrant from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/George_V_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="George V of the United Kingdom">George V</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup></p>

<tr style="height:2px">
<td colspan="2"></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td class="navbox-abovebelow" colspan="2">
<div>The generations indicate descent from <a href="/wiki/George_I_of_Great_Britain" title="George I of Great Britain">George I</a>, who formalised the use of the titles <i>prince</i> and <i>princess</i> for members of the British royal family. Where a princess may have been or is descended from George I more than once, her most senior descent, by which she bore or bears her title, is used.</div>
</td>
